    Cloud-to-cloud lightning,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Victoria,_Australia" title="Victoria, Australia">\n          Victoria, Australia\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lightningcloudtocloud.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1080" data-file-width="1920" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lightningcloudtocloud.png/220px-Lightningcloudtocloud.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lightningcloudtocloud.png/330px-Lightningcloudtocloud.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Lightningcloudtocloud.png/440px-Lightningcloudtocloud.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lightningcloudtocloud.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Cloud-to-cloud lightning seen in\n         <a href="/wiki/Gresham,_Oregon" title="Gresham, Oregon">\n          Gresham, Oregon\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Lightning discharges may occur between areas of cloud without contacting the ground. When it occurs between two separate clouds it is known as\n       <i>\n        inter-cloud lightning\n       </i>\n       , and when it occurs between areas of differing\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_potential" title="Electric potential">\n        electric potential\n       </a>\n       within a single cloud it is known as\n       <i>\n        intra-cloud lightning\n       </i>\n       . Intra-cloud lightning is the most frequently occurring type.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GHCC_primer2_48-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-GHCC_primer2-48">\n         [48]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Intra-cloud lightning most commonly occurs between the upper\n       <a href="/wiki/Cumulonimbus_incus" title="Cumulonimbus incus">\n        anvil\n       </a>\n       portion and lower reaches of a given thunderstorm. This lightning can sometimes be observed at great distances at night as so-called "\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sheet_lightning" title="Sheet lightning">\n        sheet lightning\n       </a>\n       ". In such instances, the observer may see only a flash of light without hearing any thunder.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater,_Texas..JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2304" data-file-width="3456" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG/220px-Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG/330px-Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG/440px-Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater%2C_Texas..JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Anvil_Crawler_over_Lake_Wright_Patman_south_of_Redwater,_Texas..JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Anvil Crawler over Lake Wright Patman south of Redwater, Texas on the backside of a large area of rain associated with a cold-front\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Another term used for cloud\xe2\x80\x93cloud or cloud\xe2\x80\x93cloud\xe2\x80\x93ground lightning is "Anvil Crawler", due to the habit of charge, typically originating beneath or within the anvil and scrambling through the upper cloud layers of a thunderstorm, often generating dramatic multiple branch strokes. These are usually seen as a thunderstorm passes over the observer or begins to decay. The most vivid crawler behavior occurs in well developed thunderstorms that feature extensive rear anvil shearing.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Observational_variations">\n        Observational variations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Observational variations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Anvil crawler lightning\n        </b>\n        , sometimes called\n        <b>\n         Spider lightning\n        </b>\n        is created when leaders propagate through horizontally-extensive charge regions in mature thunderstorms, usually the stratiform regions of mesoscale convective systems. These discharges usually begin as intracloud discharges originating within the convective region; the negative leader end then propagates well into the aforementioned charge regions in the stratiform area. If the leader becomes too long, it may separate into multiple bidirectional leaders. When this happens, the positive end of the separated leader may strike the ground as a positive CG flash and/or crawl on the underside of the cloud, creating a spectacular display of lightning crawling across the sky. Ground flashes produced in this manner tend to transfer high amounts of charge, and this can trigger upward lightning flashes and upper-atmospheric lightning.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">\n         <a href="#cite_note-52">\n          [52]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/Ball_lightning" title="Ball lightning">\n          Ball lightning\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        may be an\n        <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_electricity" title="Atmospheric electricity">\n         atmospheric electrical\n        </a>\n        phenomenon, the physical nature of which is still\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Controversial" title="Controversial">\n         controversial\n        </a>\n        . The term refers to reports of\n        <a href="/wiki/Luminosity" title="Luminosity">\n         luminous\n        </a>\n        , usually\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spherical" title="Spherical">\n         spherical\n        </a>\n        objects which vary from pea-sized to several meters in diameter.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">\n         <a href="#cite_note-53">\n          [53]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        It is sometimes associated with\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thunderstorms" title="Thunderstorms">\n         thunderstorms\n        </a>\n        , but unlike lightning flashes, which last only a fraction of a second, ball lightning reportedly lasts many seconds. Ball lightning has been described by eyewitnesses but rarely recorded by\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Meteorologist" title="Meteorologist">\n         meteorologists\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">\n         <a href="#cite_note-54">\n          [54]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gsu1_55-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-gsu1-55">\n          [55]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Scientific data on natural ball lightning is scarce owing to its infrequency and unpredictability. The presumption of its existence is based on reported public sightings, and has therefore produced somewhat inconsistent findings. Brett Porter,\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">\n         <a href="#cite_note-56">\n          [56]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        wildlife ranger, reported having taken a photo at Queensland of Australia in 1987.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Bead_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Bead lightning\n        </b>\n        is the decaying stage of a lightning channel in which the\n        <a href="/wiki/Luminosity" title="Luminosity">\n         luminosity\n        </a>\n        of the channel breaks up into segments. Nearly every lightning discharge will exhibit\n        <i>\n         beading\n        </i>\n        as the channel cools immediately after a return stroke, sometimes referred to as the lightning\'s \'bead-out\' stage. \'Bead lightning\' is more properly a stage of a normal lightning discharge rather than a type of lightning in itself. Beading of a lightning channel is usually a small-scale feature, and therefore is often only apparent when the observer/camera is close to the lightning.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">\n         <a href="#cite_note-57">\n          [57]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Cloud-to-air lightning\n        </b>\n        is a lightning flash in which one end of a bidirectional leader exits the cloud, but does not result in a ground flash. Such flashes can sometimes be thought of as failed ground flashes.\n        <a href="/wiki/Upper-atmospheric_lightning#Jets" title="Upper-atmospheric lightning">\n         Blue jets and gigantic jets\n        </a>\n        are a form of cloud-to-air or cloud-to-ionosphere lightning where a leader is launched from the top of a thunderstorm.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_lightning" title="Dry lightning">\n          Dry lightning\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        is used in\n        <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">\n         Australia\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">\n         Canada\n        </a>\n        and the\n        <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n         United States\n        </a>\n        for lightning that occurs with no\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">\n         precipitation\n        </a>\n        at the surface. This type of lightning is the most common natural cause of\n        <a href="/wiki/Wildfire" title="Wildfire">\n         wildfires\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scott2000_58-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Scott2000-58">\n          [58]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pyrocumulus_cloud" title="Pyrocumulus cloud">\n         Pyrocumulus clouds\n        </a>\n        produce lightning for the same reason that it is produced by cumulonimbus clouds\n        <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n         [\n         <i>\n          <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">\n           <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">\n            citation needed\n           </span>\n          </a>\n         </i>\n         ]\n        </sup>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Forked_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Forked lightning\n        </b>\n        is cloud-to-ground lightning that exhibits branching of its path.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/Heat_lightning" title="Heat lightning">\n          Heat lightning\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        is a lightning flash that appears to produce no discernible\n        <a href="#Thunder">\n         thunder\n        </a>\n        because it occurs too far away for the thunder to be heard. The sound waves dissipate before they reach the observer.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">\n         <a href="#cite_note-59">\n          [59]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Ribbon_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Ribbon lightning\n        </b>\n        occurs in thunderstorms with high cross winds and multiple return strokes. The wind will blow each successive return stroke slightly to one side of the previous return stroke, causing a ribbon effect.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">\n         <a href="#cite_note-60">\n          [60]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Rocket lightning\n        </b>\n        is a form of cloud discharge, generally horizontal and at cloud base, with a luminous channel appearing to advance through the air with visually resolvable speed, often intermittently.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMS_Glossary_61-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-AMS_Glossary-61">\n          [61]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Sheet_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Sheet lightning\n        </b>\n        is cloud-to-cloud lightning that exhibits a diffuse brightening of the surface of a cloud, caused by the actual discharge path being hidden or too far away. The lightning itself cannot be seen by the spectator, so it appears as only a flash, or a sheet of light. The lightning may be too far away to discern individual flashes.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Smooth_channel_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Smooth channel lightning\n        </b>\n        is an informal term referring to a type of cloud-to-ground lightning strike that has no visible branching and appears like a line with smooth curves as opposed to the jagged appearance of most lightning channels. They are a form of positive lightning generally observed in or near the convective regions of severe thunderstorms in the north central United States. It is theorized that severe thunderstorms in this region obtain an "inverted tripole" charge structure in which the main positive charge region is located below the main negative charge region instead of above it, and as a result these thunderstorms generate predominantly positive cloud-to-ground lightning. The term "smooth channel lightning" is also sometimes attributed to upward ground-to-cloud lightning flashes, which are generally negative flashes initiated by upward positive leaders from tall structures.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Staccato lightning\n        </b>\n        is a cloud-to-ground lightning (CG) strike which is a short-duration stroke that (often but not always) appears as a single very bright flash and often has considerable branching.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">\n         <a href="#cite_note-62">\n          [62]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        These are often found in the visual vault area near the\n        <a href="/wiki/Mesocyclone" title="Mesocyclone">\n         mesocyclone\n        </a>\n        of rotating thunderstorms and coincides with intensification of thunderstorm\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Updraft" title="Updraft">\n         updrafts\n        </a>\n        . A similar cloud-to-cloud strike consisting of a brief flash over a small area, appearing like a blip, also occurs in a similar area of rotating updrafts.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Storm_Talk_63-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Storm_Talk-63">\n          [63]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Staccoto_Lightning.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="1255" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Staccoto_Lightning.jpg/170px-Staccoto_Lightning.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Staccoto_Lightning.jpg/255px-Staccoto_Lightning.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Staccoto_Lightning.jpg/340px-Staccoto_Lightning.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Staccoto_Lightning.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         This CG was of very short duration, exhibited highly branched channels and was very bright indicating that it was staccato lightning near New Boston, Texas.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Superbolts">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Superbolts\n        </b>\n        are bolts of lightning around a hundred times brighter than normal. On Earth, one in a million lightning strikes is a superbolt.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">\n         <a href="#cite_note-64">\n          [64]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">\n         <a href="#cite_note-65">\n          [65]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Sympathetic_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Sympathetic lightning\n        </b>\n        is the tendency of lightning to be loosely coordinated across long distances. Discharges can appear in clusters when viewed from space.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       <span id="Clear-air_lightning">\n       </span>\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Upward lightning\n        </b>\n        or\n        <b>\n         ground-to-cloud lightning\n        </b>\n        is a lightning flash which originates from the top of a grounded object and propagates upward from this point. This type of lightning can be triggered by a preceding lightning flash, or it may initiate entirely on its own. The former is generally found in regions where spider lightning occurs, and may involve multiple grounded objects simultaneously. The latter usually occurs during the cold season and may be the dominant lightning type in thundersnow events.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">\n         <a href="#cite_note-66">\n          [66]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Clear-air lightning\n        </b>\n        describes lightning that occurs with no apparent cloud close enough to have produced it. In the U.S. and Canadian\n        <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Mountains" title="Rocky Mountains">\n         Rockies\n        </a>\n        , a thunderstorm can be in an adjacent valley and not observable from the valley where the lightning bolt strikes, either visually or audibly. European and Asian mountainous areas experience similar events. Also in areas such as\n        <a href="/wiki/Sound_(geography)" title="Sound (geography)">\n         sounds\n        </a>\n        , large lakes or open plains, when the storm cell is on the near horizon (within 26 kilometres (16\xc2\xa0mi)) there may be some distant activity, a strike can occur and as the storm is so far away, the strike is referred to as\n        <b>\n         a bolt from the blue\n        </b>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">\n         <a href="#cite_note-67">\n          [67]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        These flashes usually begin as normal intracloud lightning flashes before the negative leader exits the cloud and strikes the ground a considerable distance away.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-onlinelibrary.wiley.com_50-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-onlinelibrary.wiley.com-50">\n          [50]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Krehbiel.2C_P._R._2008_51-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Krehbiel.2C_P._R._2008-51">\n          [51]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        Positive clear-air strikes can occur in highly-sheared environments where the upper positive charge region becomes horizontally displaced from the precipitation area.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">\n         <a href="#cite_note-68">\n          [68]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Effects">\n        Effects\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Effects">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lightning_strike">\n        Lightning strike\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Lightning strike">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning_strike" title="Lightning strike">\n        Lightning strike\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Objects struck by lightning experience heat and magnetic forces of great magnitude. The heat created by lightning currents traveling through a tree may vaporize its sap, causing a steam explosion that bursts the trunk. As lightning travels through sandy soil, the soil surrounding the\n       <a href="/wiki/Plasma_channel" title="Plasma channel">\n        plasma channel\n       </a>\n       may melt, forming tubular structures called\n       <a href="/wiki/Fulgurite" title="Fulgurite">\n        fulgurites\n       </a>\n       . Even though roughly 90 percent of people struck by lightning survive,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Outside_2014-09-22_69-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Outside_2014-09-22-69">\n         [69]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       humans or animals struck by lightning may suffer severe injury due to internal organ and nervous system damage. Buildings or tall structures hit by lightning may be damaged as the lightning seeks unintended paths to ground. By safely conducting a lightning strike to ground, a lightning protection system can greatly reduce the probability of severe property damage. Lightning also serves an important role in the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen_cycle" title="Nitrogen cycle">\n        nitrogen cycle\n       </a>\n       by oxidizing diatomic nitrogen in the air into\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nitrates" title="Nitrates">\n        nitrates\n       </a>\n       which are deposited by rain and can fertilize the growth of plants and other organisms.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">\n        <a href="#cite_note-70">\n         [70]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">\n        <a href="#cite_note-71">\n         [71]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Thunder">\n        Thunder\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Thunder">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunder" title="Thunder">\n        Thunder\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Because the electrostatic discharge of terrestrial lightning superheats the air to plasma temperatures along the length of the discharge channel in a short duration,\n       <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_theory_of_gases" title="Kinetic theory of gases">\n        kinetic theory\n       </a>\n       dictates gaseous molecules undergo a rapid increase in pressure and thus expand outward from the lightning creating a\n       <a href="/wiki/Shock_wave" title="Shock wave">\n        shock wave\n       </a>\n       audible as thunder. Since the sound waves propagate not from a single point source but along the length of the lightning\'s path, the sound origin\'s varying distances from the observer can generate a rolling or rumbling effect. Perception of the sonic characteristics is further complicated by factors such as the irregular and possibly branching geometry of the lightning channel, by\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Echo_(phenomenon)" title="Echo (phenomenon)">\n        acoustic echoing\n       </a>\n       from terrain, and by the typically multiple-stroke characteristic of the lightning strike.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_light" title="Speed of light">\n        Light travels\n       </a>\n       at about 300,000,000\xc2\xa0m/s, and\n       <a href="/wiki/Speed_of_sound" title="Speed of sound">\n        sound\n       </a>\n       travels through air at about 340\xc2\xa0m/s. An observer can approximate the distance to the strike by timing the interval between the visible lightning and the audible thunder it generates. A lightning flash preceding its thunder by one second would be approximately 340 metres (0.21\xc2\xa0mi) in distance; a delay of three seconds would indicate a distance of about one kilometer (0.62\xc2\xa0mi) (3\xc3\x97340\xc2\xa0m). A flash preceding thunder by five seconds would indicate a distance of approximately one mile (1.6\xc2\xa0km) (5\xc3\x97340\xc2\xa0m). Consequently, a lightning strike observed at a very close distance will be accompanied by a sudden clap of thunder, with almost no perceptible time lapse, possibly accompanied by the smell of\n       <a href="/wiki/Ozone" title="Ozone">\n        ozone\n       </a>\n       (O\n       <sub>\n        3\n       </sub>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="High-energy_radiation">\n        High-energy radiation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: High-energy radiation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The production of\n       <a href="/wiki/X-ray" title="X-ray">\n        X-rays\n       </a>\n       by a bolt of lightning was theoretically predicted as early as 1925\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">\n        <a href="#cite_note-72">\n         [72]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but no evidence was found until 2001/2002,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">\n        <a href="#cite_note-73">\n         [73]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">\n        <a href="#cite_note-74">\n         [74]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">\n        <a href="#cite_note-75">\n         [75]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       when researchers at the\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico_Institute_of_Mining_and_Technology" title="New Mexico Institute of Mining and Technology">\n        New Mexico Institute of Mining and Technology\n       </a>\n       detected X-ray emissions from an induced lightning strike along a grounded wire trailed behind a rocket shot into a storm cloud. In the same year\n       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">\n        University of Florida\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Florida_Institute_of_Technology" title="Florida Institute of Technology">\n        Florida Tech\n       </a>\n       researchers used an array of electric field and X-ray detectors at a lightning research facility in North Florida to confirm that natural lightning makes X-rays in large quantities during the propagation of stepped leaders. The cause of the X-ray emissions is still a matter for research, as the temperature of lightning is too low to account for the X-rays observed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">\n        <a href="#cite_note-76">\n         [76]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sergio2013_77-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Sergio2013-77">\n         [77]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A number of observations by space-based telescopes have revealed even higher energy\n       <a href="/wiki/Gamma_ray" title="Gamma ray">\n        gamma ray\n       </a>\n       emissions, the so-called\n       <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_gamma-ray_flash" title="Terrestrial gamma-ray flash">\n        terrestrial gamma-ray flashes\n       </a>\n       (TGFs). These observations pose a challenge to current theories of lightning, especially with the recent discovery of the clear signatures of\n       <a href="/wiki/Antimatter" title="Antimatter">\n        antimatter\n       </a>\n       produced in lightning.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78">\n        <a href="#cite_note-78">\n         [78]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Recent research has shown that secondary species, produced by these TGFs, such as\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electrons" title="Electrons">\n        electrons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Positrons" title="Positrons">\n        positrons\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Neutrons" title="Neutrons">\n        neutrons\n       </a>\n       or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protons" title="Protons">\n        protons\n       </a>\n       , can gain energies of up to several tens of MeV.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KohnEbert_79-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KohnEbert-79">\n         [79]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-KohnHarakeh_80-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-KohnHarakeh-80">\n         [80]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Volcanic">\n        Volcanic\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Volcanic">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rinjani_1994.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="519" data-file-width="800" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Rinjani_1994.jpg/220px-Rinjani_1994.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Rinjani_1994.jpg/330px-Rinjani_1994.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f2/Rinjani_1994.jpg/440px-Rinjani_1994.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rinjani_1994.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Volcanic material thrust high into the atmosphere can trigger lightning.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Volcanic activity produces lightning-friendly conditions in multiple ways. The enormous quantity of pulverized material and gases explosively ejected into the atmosphere creates a dense plume of particles. The ash density and constant motion within the volcanic plume produces charge by frictional interactions (triboelectrification), resulting in very powerful and very frequent flashes as the cloud attempts to neutralize itself. Due to the extensive solid material (ash) content, unlike the water rich charge generating zones of a normal thundercloud, it is often called a\n       <a href="/wiki/Dirty_thunderstorm" title="Dirty thunderstorm">\n        dirty thunderstorm\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        Powerful and frequent flashes have been witnessed in the volcanic plume as far back as the 79 AD eruption of\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vesuvius" title="Vesuvius">\n         Vesuvius\n        </a>\n        by\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pliny_The_Younger" title="Pliny The Younger">\n         Pliny The Younger\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Volcano_Lightning_81-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Volcano_Lightning-81">\n          [81]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Likewise, vapors and ash originating from vents on the volcano\'s flanks may produce more localized and smaller flashes upwards of 2.9\xc2\xa0km long.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Small, short duration\n        <a href="/wiki/Electric_spark" title="Electric spark">\n         sparks\n        </a>\n        , recently documented near newly extruded magma, attest to the material being highly charged prior to even entering the atmosphere.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82">\n         <a href="#cite_note-82">\n          [82]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extraterrestrial">\n        Extraterrestrial\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Extraterrestrial">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       Lightning has been observed within the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celestial_body_atmosphere" title="Celestial body atmosphere">\n        atmospheres\n       </a>\n       of other\n       <a href="/wiki/Planet" title="Planet">\n        planets\n       </a>\n       , such as\n       <a href="/wiki/Jupiter" title="Jupiter">\n        Jupiter\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Saturn" title="Saturn">\n        Saturn\n       </a>\n       . Although in the minority on Earth, superbolts appear to be common on Jupiter.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lightning on Venus has been a controversial subject after decades of study. During the Soviet\n       <a href="/wiki/Venera" title="Venera">\n        Venera\n       </a>\n       and U.S.\n       <a href="/wiki/Pioneer_program" title="Pioneer program">\n        Pioneer\n       </a>\n       missions of the 1970s and 1980s, signals suggesting lightning may be present in the upper atmosphere were detected.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-plasma_83-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-plasma-83">\n         [83]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Although the\n       <a href="/wiki/Cassini%E2%80%93Huygens" title="Cassini\xe2\x80\x93Huygens">\n        Cassini\xe2\x80\x93Huygens\n       </a>\n       mission fly-by of Venus in 1999 detected no signs of lightning, the observation window lasted mere hours. Radio pulses recorded by the spacecraft\n       <a href="/wiki/Venus_Express" title="Venus Express">\n        Venus Express\n       </a>\n       (which began orbiting Venus in April 2006) may originate from lightning on Venus.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Human-related_phenomena">\n        Human-related phenomena\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Human-related phenomena">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Airplane contrails\n        </b>\n        have also been observed to influence lightning to a small degree. The water vapor-dense contrails of airplanes may provide a lower resistance pathway through the atmosphere having some influence upon the establishment of an ionic pathway for a lightning flash to follow.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84">\n         <a href="#cite_note-84">\n          [84]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Rocket exhaust plumes\n        </b>\n        provided a pathway for lightning when it was witnessed striking the\n        <a href="/wiki/Apollo_12" title="Apollo 12">\n         Apollo 12 rocket\n        </a>\n        shortly after takeoff.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         <a href="/wiki/Thermonuclear_weapon" title="Thermonuclear weapon">\n          Thermonuclear explosions\n         </a>\n        </b>\n        by providing extra material for electrical conduction and a very turbulent localized atmosphere, have been seen triggering lightning flashes within the mushroom cloud. In addition, intense gamma radiation from large nuclear explosions may develop intensely charged regions in the surrounding air through\n        <a href="/wiki/Compton_scattering" title="Compton scattering">\n         Compton scattering\n        </a>\n        . The intensely charged space charge regions create multiple clear-air lightning discharges shortly after the device detonates.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nuclear_Lightning_85-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-Nuclear_Lightning-85">\n          [85]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_study">\n        Scientific study\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Scientific study">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">\n        Properties\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Properties">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Thunder is heard as a rolling, gradually dissipating rumble because the sound from different portions of a long stroke arrives at slightly different times.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_86-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-86">\n         [86]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When the local electric field exceeds the\n       <a href="/wiki/Dielectric_strength" title="Dielectric strength">\n        dielectric strength\n       </a>\n       of damp air (about 3 million volts per meter), electrical discharge results in a\n       <i>\n        strike\n       </i>\n       , often followed by commensurate discharges branching from the same path. (See image, right.) Mechanisms that cause the charges to build up to lightning are still a matter of scientific investigation.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-how_87-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-how-87">\n         [87]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-noaa_88-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-noaa-88">\n         [88]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       New study confirming dielectric breakdown is involved.\n       <a class="external text" href="http://www.nature.com/ncomms/2016/160215/ncomms10721/full/ncomms10721.html?WT.ec_id=NCOMMS-20160217" rel="nofollow">\n        Rison 2016\n       </a>\n       . Lightning may be caused by the circulation of warm moisture-filled air through\n       <a href="/wiki/Electric_field" title="Electric field">\n        electric fields\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">\n        <a href="#cite_note-89">\n         [89]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Ice or water particles then accumulate charge as in a\n       <a href="/wiki/Van_de_Graaff_generator" title="Van de Graaff generator">\n        Van de Graaff generator\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">\n        <a href="#cite_note-90">\n         [90]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Researchers at the University of Florida found that the final one-dimensional speeds of 10 flashes observed were between 1.0\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n         5\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       and 1.4\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n         6\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       m/s, with an average of 4.4\n       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">\n        \xc3\x97\n       </span>\n       10\n       <sup>\n        <span style="white-space:nowrap">\n         5\n        </span>\n       </sup>\n       m/s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">\n        <a href="#cite_note-91">\n         [91]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Detection_and_monitoring">\n        Detection and monitoring\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Detection and monitoring">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="164" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG/220px-Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG/330px-Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/93/Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG/440px-Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Museu_Rom%C3%A0ntic_Can_Papiol._Maig_2014_05.JPG" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning strike counter in a museum\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning_detection" title="Lightning detection">\n        Lightning detection\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The earliest detector invented to warn of the approach of a thunder storm was the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lightning_bell" title="Lightning bell">\n        lightning bell\n       </a>\n       .\n       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">\n        Benjamin Franklin\n       </a>\n       installed one such device in his house.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">\n        <a href="#cite_note-92">\n         [92]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">\n        <a href="#cite_note-93">\n         [93]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The detector was based on an electrostatic device called the \'electric chimes\' invented by\n       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Gordon_(Benedictine)" title="Andrew Gordon (Benedictine)">\n        Andrew Gordon\n       </a>\n       in 1742.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lightning discharges generate a wide range of electromagnetic radiations, including radio-frequency pulses. The times at which a pulse from a given lightning discharge arrives at several receivers can be used to locate the source of the discharge. The United States federal government has constructed a nationwide grid of such lightning detectors, allowing lightning discharges to be tracked in real time throughout the continental U.S.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">\n        <a href="#cite_note-94">\n         [94]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">\n        <a href="#cite_note-95">\n         [95]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Earth-ionosphere_waveguide" title="Earth-ionosphere waveguide">\n        Earth-ionosphere waveguide\n       </a>\n       traps electromagnetic\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/VLF" title="VLF">\n        VLF\n       </a>\n       - and\n       <a href="/wiki/Extremely_low_frequency" title="Extremely low frequency">\n        ELF\n       </a>\n       waves. Electromagnetic pulses transmitted by lightning strikes propagate within that waveguide. The waveguide is dispersive, which means that their\n       <a href="/wiki/Group_velocity" title="Group velocity">\n        group velocity\n       </a>\n       depends on frequency. The difference of the group time delay of a lightning pulse at adjacent frequencies is proportional to the distance between transmitter and receiver. Together with direction finding methods, this allows to locate lightning strikes up to distances of 10,000\xc2\xa0km from their origin. Moreover, the eigenfrequencies of the Earth-ionospheric waveguide, the\n       <a href="/wiki/Schumann_resonances" title="Schumann resonances">\n        Schumann resonances\n       </a>\n       at about 7.5\xc2\xa0Hz, are used to determine the global thunderstorm activity.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">\n        <a href="#cite_note-96">\n         [96]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In addition to ground-based lightning detection, several instruments aboard satellites have been constructed to observe lightning distribution. These include the Optical Transient Detector (OTD), aboard the OrbView-1 satellite launched on April 3, 1995, and the subsequent Lightning Imaging Sensor (LIS) aboard\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TRMM" title="TRMM">\n        TRMM\n       </a>\n       launched on November 28, 1997.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-n1_97-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-n1-97">\n         [97]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-n2_98-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-n2-98">\n         [98]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-n3_99-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-n3-99">\n         [99]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Artificially_triggered">\n        Artificially triggered\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Artificially triggered">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Rocket-triggered lightning\n        </b>\n        can be "triggered" by launching\n        <a href="/wiki/Lightning_rocket" title="Lightning rocket">\n         specially designed rockets\n        </a>\n        trailing spools of wire into thunderstorms. The wire unwinds as the rocket ascends, creating an elevated ground that can attract descending leaders. If a leader attaches, the wire provides a low-resistance pathway for a lightning flash to occur. The wire is vaporized by the return current flow, creating a straight lightning plasma channel in its place. This method allows for scientific research of lightning to occur under a more controlled and predictable manner.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vid_100-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-vid-100">\n          [100]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <dl>\n         <dd>\n          The International Center for Lightning Research and Testing (ICLRT) at Camp Blanding, Florida typically uses rocket triggered lightning in their research studies.\n         </dd>\n        </dl>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <b>\n         Laser-triggered\n        </b>\n        <dl>\n         <dd>\n          Since the 1970s,\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">\n           <a href="#cite_note-101">\n            [101]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">\n           <a href="#cite_note-102">\n            [102]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">\n           <a href="#cite_note-103">\n            [103]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">\n           <a href="#cite_note-104">\n            [104]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-harv_105-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-harv-105">\n            [105]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">\n           <a href="#cite_note-106">\n            [106]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          researchers have attempted to trigger lightning strikes by means of infrared or ultraviolet lasers, which create a channel of ionized gas through which the lightning would be conducted to ground. Such triggering of lightning is intended to protect rocket launching pads, electric power facilities, and other sensitive targets.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">\n           <a href="#cite_note-107">\n            [107]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-njop_108-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-njop-108">\n            [108]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-joot_109-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-joot-109">\n            [109]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apl_110-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-apl-110">\n            [110]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-osaka_111-0">\n           <a href="#cite_note-osaka-111">\n            [111]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </dd>\n         <dd>\n          In New Mexico, U.S., scientists tested a new\n          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Terawatt" title="Terawatt">\n           terawatt\n          </a>\n          laser which provoked lightning. Scientists fired ultra-fast pulses from an extremely powerful laser thus sending several terawatts into the clouds to call down electrical discharges in storm clouds over the region. The laser beams sent from the laser make channels of ionized molecules known as "\n          <b>\n           filaments\n          </b>\n          ". Before the lightning strikes earth, the filaments lead electricity through the clouds, playing the role of lightning rods. Researchers generated filaments that lived a period too short to trigger a real lightning strike. Nevertheless, a boost in electrical activity within the clouds was registered. According to the French and German scientists who ran the experiment, the fast pulses sent from the laser will be able to provoke lightning strikes on demand.\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">\n           <a href="#cite_note-112">\n            [112]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n          Statistical analysis showed that their laser pulses indeed enhanced the electrical activity in the thundercloud where it was aimed\xe2\x80\x94in effect they generated small local discharges located at the position of the\n          <a href="/wiki/Plasma_channel" title="Plasma channel">\n           plasma channels\n          </a>\n          .\n          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">\n           <a href="#cite_note-113">\n            [113]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </dd>\n        </dl>\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_manifestations">\n        Physical manifestations\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Physical manifestations">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="452" data-file-width="311" height="247" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4d/LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg/170px-LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4d/LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg/255px-LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/4/4d/LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg 2x" width="170"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:LIRM_anomaly_with_archaeological_hearths.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning-induced remanent magnetization (LIRM) mapped during a magnetic field gradient survey of an archaeological site located in Wyoming, United States.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <h4>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Magnetism">\n        Magnetism\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Magnetism">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h4>\n      <p>\n       The movement of electrical charges produces a magnetic field (see\n       <a href="/wiki/Electromagnetism" title="Electromagnetism">\n        electromagnetism\n       </a>\n       ). The intense currents of a lightning discharge create a fleeting but very strong magnetic field. Where the lightning current path passes through rock, soil, or metal these materials can become permanently magnetized. This effect is known as lightning-induced\n       <a href="/wiki/Remanence" title="Remanence">\n        remanent\n       </a>\n       magnetism, or LIRM. These currents follow the least resistive path, often horizontally near the surface\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">\n        <a href="#cite_note-114">\n         [114]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">\n        <a href="#cite_note-115">\n         [115]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       but sometimes vertically, where faults, ore bodies, or ground water offers a less resistive path.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">\n        <a href="#cite_note-116">\n         [116]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       One theory suggests that\n       <a href="/wiki/Lodestone" title="Lodestone">\n        lodestones\n       </a>\n       , natural magnets encountered in ancient times, were created in this manner.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117">\n        <a href="#cite_note-117">\n         [117]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Lightning-induced magnetic anomalies can be mapped in the ground,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">\n        <a href="#cite_note-118">\n         [118]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">\n        <a href="#cite_note-119">\n         [119]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and analysis of magnetized materials can confirm lightning was the source of the magnetization\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">\n        <a href="#cite_note-120">\n         [120]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and provide an estimate of the peak current of the lightning discharge.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">\n        <a href="#cite_note-121">\n         [121]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Solar_wind_and_cosmic_rays">\n        Solar wind and cosmic rays\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Solar wind and cosmic rays">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Some high energy cosmic rays produced by supernovas as well as solar particles from the solar wind, enter the atmosphere and electrify the air, which may create pathways for lightning bolts.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">\n        <a href="#cite_note-122">\n         [122]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="In_culture_and_religion">\n        In culture and religion\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: In culture and religion">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Further information:\n       <a href="/wiki/Lightning_in_religion" title="Lightning in religion">\n        Lightning in religion\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1233" data-file-width="1600" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg/220px-Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg/330px-Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg/440px-Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis_-_LIGHTNING_-_1909.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Lightning by\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mikalojus_Konstantinas_Ciurlionis" title="Mikalojus Konstantinas Ciurlionis">\n          Mikalojus Konstantinas Ciurlionis\n         </a>\n         (1909)\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       In many cultures, lightning has been viewed as part of a deity or a deity in and of itself. These include the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Greek_god" title="Greek god">\n        Greek god\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">\n        Zeus\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Aztec" title="Aztec">\n        Aztec\n       </a>\n       god\n       <a href="/wiki/Tlaloc" title="Tlaloc">\n        Tlaloc\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Maya_religion" title="Maya religion">\n        Mayan\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/God_K" title="God K">\n        God K\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_mythology" title="Slavic mythology">\n        Slavic mythology\n       </a>\n       \'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Perun" title="Perun">\n        Perun\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Baltic_languages" title="Baltic languages">\n        Baltic\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/P%C4%93rkons" title="P\xc4\x93rkons">\n        P\xc4\x93rkons\n       </a>\n       /\n       <a href="/wiki/Perk%C5%ABnas" title="Perk\xc5\xabnas">\n        Perk\xc5\xabnas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Thor" title="Thor">\n        Thor\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">\n        Norse mythology\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <a href="/wiki/Ukko" title="Ukko">\n        Ukko\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Finnish_mythology" title="Finnish mythology">\n        Finnish mythology\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Hindu" title="Hindu">\n        Hindu\n       </a>\n       god\n       <a href="/wiki/Indra" title="Indra">\n        Indra\n       </a>\n       , and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Shinto" title="Shinto">\n        Shinto\n       </a>\n       god\n       <a href="/wiki/Raijin" title="Raijin">\n        Raijin\n       </a>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">\n        <a href="#cite_note-123">\n         [123]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In the traditional religion of the African\n       <a href="/wiki/Bantu_peoples" title="Bantu peoples">\n        Bantu\n       </a>\n       tribes, lightning is a sign of the ire of the gods. Verses in the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">\n        Jewish\n       </a>\n       religion and in\n       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">\n        Islam\n       </a>\n       also ascribe supernatural importance to lightning. In\n       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">\n        Christianity\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_Coming" title="Second Coming">\n        Second Coming\n       </a>\n       of\n       <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">\n        Jesus\n       </a>\n       is compared to lightning.\n       <sup class="nourlexpansion reference">\n        <a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Matthew+24%3A27&amp;version=NRSV" rel="nofollow">\n         [Matthew 24:27]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="nourlexpansion reference">\n        <a class="external text" href="https://www.biblegateway.com/passage/?search=Luke+17%3A24&amp;version=NRSV" rel="nofollow">\n         [Luke 17:24]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The expression "Lightning never strikes twice (in the same place)" is similar to "Opportunity never knocks twice" in the vein of a "once in a lifetime" opportunity,\n       <i>\n        i.e.\n       </i>\n       , something that is generally considered improbable. Lightning occurs frequently and more so in specific areas. Since various factors alter the\n       <a href="/wiki/Probability" title="Probability">\n        probability\n       </a>\n       of strikes at any given location, repeat lightning strikes have a very low probability (but are not impossible).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-uman2_124-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-uman2-124">\n         [124]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">\n        <a href="#cite_note-125">\n         [125]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Similarly, "A bolt from the blue" refers to something totally unexpected.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Some political parties use lightning flashes as a symbol of power, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Action_Party" title="People\'s Action Party">\n        People\'s Action Party\n       </a>\n       in\n       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">\n        Singapore\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/British_Union_of_Fascists" title="British Union of Fascists">\n        British Union of Fascists\n       </a>\n       during the 1930s, and the\n       <a href="/wiki/National_States%27_Rights_Party" title="National States\' Rights Party">\n        National States\' Rights Party\n       </a>\n       in the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n        United States\n       </a>\n       during the 1950s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">\n        <a href="#cite_note-126">\n         [126]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The\n       <a href="/wiki/Schutzstaffel" title="Schutzstaffel">\n        Schutzstaffel\n       </a>\n       , the\n       <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">\n        paramilitary\n       </a>\n       wing of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">\n        Nazi Party\n       </a>\n       , used the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sig_(rune)" title="Sig (rune)">\n        Sig rune\n       </a>\n       in their logo which symbolizes lightning. The\n       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">\n        German\n       </a>\n       word\n       <a href="/wiki/Blitzkrieg" title="Blitzkrieg">\n        Blitzkrieg\n       </a>\n       , which means "lightning war", was a major offensive strategy of the German army during\n       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">\n        World War II\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">\n        French\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Italian_language" title="Italian language">\n        Italian\n       </a>\n       , the expression for "Love at first sight" is\n       <i>\n        coup de foudre\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        colpo di fulmine\n       </i>\n       , respectively, which literally translated means "lightning strike". Some European languages have a separate word for lightning which strikes the ground (as opposed to lightning in general); often it is a\n       <a href="/wiki/Cognate" title="Cognate">\n        cognate\n       </a>\n       of the English word "rays". The name of\n       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">\n        New Zealand\n       </a>\n       \'s most celebrated\n       <a href="/wiki/Thoroughbred" title="Thoroughbred">\n        thoroughbred\n       </a>\n       horse,\n       <a href="/wiki/Phar_Lap" title="Phar Lap">\n        Phar Lap\n       </a>\n       , derives from the shared\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_Zhuang" title="Standard Zhuang">\n        Zhuang\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Thai_language" title="Thai language">\n        Thai\n       </a>\n       word for lightning.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">\n        <a href="#cite_note-127">\n         [127]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The bolt of lightning in\n       <a href="/wiki/Heraldry" title="Heraldry">\n        heraldry\n       </a>\n       is called a\n       <a href="/wiki/Thunderbolt" title="Thunderbolt">\n        thunderbolt\n       </a>\n       and is shown as a zigzag with non-pointed ends. This symbol usually represents power and speed.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The lightning bolt is used to represent the instantaneous communication capabilities of electrically powered\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Telegraph" title="Telegraph">\n        telegraphs\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Radio" title="Radio">\n        radios\n       </a>\n       . It was a commonly used motif in\n       <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">\n        Art Deco\n       </a>\n       design, especially the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Zig-zag" title="Zig-zag">\n        zig-zag\n       </a>\n       Art Deco design of the late 1920s.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">\n        <a href="#cite_note-128">\n         [128]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The lightning bolt is a common insignia for\n       <a href="/wiki/Military_communications" title="Military communications">\n        military communications\n       </a>\n       units throughout the world. A lightning bolt is also the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NATO_Military_Symbols_for_Land_Based_Systems" title="NATO Military Symbols for Land Based Systems">\n        NATO symbol for a signal asset\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The Unicode symbol for lightning is \xe2\x98\x87 U+2607\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">\n        See also\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lightning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: See also">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dinosaur_lightning.JPG">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1296" data-file-width="1944" height="147" href="/wiki/Petrified_Forest_National_Park" title="Petrified Forest National Park">\n          Petrified Forest National Park\n         </a>\n         , USA\n        </div>\n       </div>\n  </a>\n         </span>\n         <span class="reference-text">\n          <cite class="citation web">\n           <a class="external text"
